- **2026-07-19** ‚Äî **AT-267 Assistants audit + partial remediation (branch `QA2`, NOT deployed).** Audited the merged Assistants feature (`.ai/audits/assistants-feature-audit-2026-07-19.md`): the security CORE is excellent (live permission intersection never escalates; four-layer property-upload hard lock; zero-grant role routed before role resolution; owner/assistant-of-assistant/inactive excluded as agents; one-agent unique via generated column; branch+agency scoped; soft-delete-as-archive). But only Prompts A‚ÄìF+K shipped, and four gaps found ‚Äî two material. **Fixed + Tinker-verified (3 of 4):** (1) **admin features now default OFF** for an assistant of an admin ‚Äî Johan's explicit ask ‚Äî via `config/assistants.php ‚Üí admin_default_off_sections` (catalogue-`section`-driven, not a hand-list) seeded `granted=false` in `AssistantMatrixSnapshotService::seed()`; ordinary keys stay ON, property lock untouched. (2) **The `on_behalf_of_user_id` audit trail (spec ¬ß11, the compliance spine) was entirely unbuilt** ‚Äî now `App\Support\ActingFor` (mirrors AT-118 Impersonation) + `StampsOnBehalfOf` trait on 9 audit models + nullable column on all 10 ¬ß11 tables + the 2 raw writers (RecordDomainEvent, PropertyAuditService marketing-share) + the missing `ContactAccessLog::impersonator()` relation + a new `AuditActorCoverageTest` ratchet (NO_STAFF_ACTOR + PENDING_COVERAGE buckets). Verified: assistant's audit write stamps on_behalf=agent, normal write null, ratchet green, domain_event_log has the column. (4b) `assistants:sync-matrix` drift command built + scheduled 04:15. **Deliberately NOT done (deferred to a render/test-capable lane, Johan's call):** (4a) full profile stripping (spec ¬ß10 ‚Äî ~15 `@unless($isAssistant)` gates across the 1,415-line `agent/portal.blade.php` + a NEW Proof-of-Residence card + `computeComplianceStatus()` changes; a missed section leaks bank/commission/FFC ‚Üí must be verified by RENDERING) and (3) record-ownership routing (`ownershipUserId()` is dead on writes; wiring it changes where commission/pipeline land ‚Üí money-sensitive, per-surface, hard to reverse). No phpunit in this lane; run `tests/Feature/Assistants/*` + `AuditActorCoverageTest` before merge/deploy. **The rule: an audit-fix that ships untested POPIA-UI or money-routing is worse than the gap it closes ‚Äî defer those to where they can be verified.**

- **2026-07-19** ‚Äî **Branch-split coverage pass ‚Äî closed most of the isolation debt register the way the audit said to, not the way that would have hidden agents' own commission.** Re-verified the split mechanism (`.ai/audits/branch-split-verification-2026-07-19.md`): scopes/gate-parity/view_all-bypass/NULL-handling/write-stamping all correct and consistent ‚Äî the only gap was *coverage*. Fixed the safe clusters with Johan's sign-off. **The design key that made it safe:** every model scoped this pass has an owning `user_id`/`captured_by_user_id` or a branch-carrying parent, so branch is inherited from that OWNER/PARENT via `InheritsBranchFromParent` ‚Äî **context-independent**, so a write from a queue/console/observer with no auth user still stamps the right branch. That is what defused **CommissionLedger (MONEY)**: the na√Øve `BelongsToBranch` acting-user stamp NULLs in queue/console and would hide an agent's own commission under Split ON; instead it inherits the **earning agent's** branch (`user_id`) ‚Äî Tinker-proven in a no-auth context that the row stamps the earner's branch, another branch can't see it, and the earner still can. **5 migrations, all backfilled:** `branch_id` added to the DealV2 per-deal children (activity log, distributions, remarks, stage moves, escalations, step instances, settlements, step comments/documents ‚Äî inherit ‚Üê deal/step) + the buyer-match models (‚Üê Contact/Property/ProspectingListing) + ProspectingListing (‚Üê capturing agent) + Worksheet (‚Üê owner); trait added to the already-`branch_id` Target/ActivityTarget/DailyActivity/DailyActivityEntry (‚Üê User) + MonthlyTargetGoal (branch set explicitly). **`DealDocumentAccessLog` deliberately left alone** ‚Äî append-only immutable POPIA evidence log, documented as not read-scoped (reads always via an owned distribution). **Decay-stopper (`BranchSplitIsolationTest`):** Whistleblow + AgencyComplianceProvision ‚Üí `SHARED_BY_DESIGN` (Johan: agency-wide); `PENDING_DECISION` 14 ‚Üí 6, ratchet tightened to `<= 6`. Remaining 6 are real open questions (AgentApplication public-portal write; ToolHistoryEntry; TvAccessCode/TvMessage have no `agency_id`; ListingImportRun/Snapshot). **Verified in-lane** (no PHPUnit here): `php -l` clean on 20 models + 5 migrations, all migrations ran + backfilled, `schema:dump` refreshed, Tinker replicated the decay-stopper (every `branch_id` model classified) + proved stamping/isolation. **MUST before merge/deploy:** run `BranchSplitIsolationTest` + suite on a test-capable lane; the 5 migrations must run on Staging/live before any agency with existing data flips Split ON. Branch `QA2`, NOT deployed, NOT committed. **The rule: don't scope a money table on the acting user ‚Äî inherit the earning agent's branch, or you hide people's own commission from them.**

- **2026-07-18** ‚Äî **The onboarding wizard walked 12 steps of settings and never once showed the Admin the SHAPE of the product.** Feature on/off switches existed but were scattered ‚Äî `marketing_enabled`/syndication inside the Properties step, `matches_enabled` inside Matches, `split_branches_enabled` inside Branches, and `website_enabled` **nowhere in the wizard at all** (agency-edit only). Built a new **step 2 ‚Äî the feature switchboard**: "What CoreX can do ‚Äî turn features on or off", six toggles (Marketing ¬∑ Publish to Property24 ¬∑ Publish to Private Property ¬∑ Core Matches ¬∑ Multi-branch offices ¬∑ Public website), each with a full plain-English `explain` and a concrete "What this changes:" `affects`, grouped with a "Property portals" sub-heading. **It writes LIVE through the EXISTING canonical savers** ‚Äî the same `SettingsController@updateMarketingEnabled`/`updateSyndicationPortals`/`updateMatchesEnabled`/`updateSplitBranches` + `AgencyApiKeyController@toggleWebsite` the settings page uses ‚Äî never a parallel flag system (spec ¬ß3.1). **Two structural consequences.** (1) **One home per switch:** the 5 masters moved OUT of their detail steps into the switchboard; the detail steps keep only how-it-works config. (2) **Adaptive setup:** a feature turned OFF **skips its dedicated detail step** ‚Äî v1 gates the whole `matches` step on `matches_enabled`, built generic (`AgencyOnboardingSetup::stepGates()`/`activeSteps($agency)`) so future feature-steps gate by adding one entry; nav/advance/show/progress all iterate ACTIVE steps, and the progress **denominator became the active-step count** so 100% stays reachable without ever configuring a feature you turned off. **The landmine, fixed as a class (BUILD_STANDARD ¬ß6):** fanning a toggle to a saver makes it a multi-caller, and 4 of the 5 reused savers coerced an **absent** checkbox to `false` (bare `$request->boolean()`) ‚Äî the exact ¬ß6.1 trap that silently wiped `weekend_visible`/`ss_show_complex_section` before. Hardened all four to `$request->has()` guards (absent ‚áí leave alone; the switchboard + settings forms both post a hidden `"0"` companion so rendered-but-unchecked still saves false); `toggleWebsite` was already safe (`required|boolean`). Verified: **the switchboard blade uses the wizard's existing data-driven toggle renderer** (already carries the hidden companion + explain/affects + copy-guard) plus a new optional `heading` for the portal grouping ‚Äî no bespoke partial that re-reads values, so there's nothing to drift (a small deliberate deviation from the spec's ¬ß5.2 "dedicated partial", noted because the generic renderer already IS the card layout). No migration (every toggle reuses an existing store: `PerformanceSetting` keys + `agencies` columns). Tests `AgencySetupFeatureSwitchboardTest` **10/10** (renders six toggles + `what` card, round-trips each toggle into the real store == settings-page result, `website_enabled` round-trips, matches-off drops the step from `activeSteps`/redirects/advances-past/excludes-from-denominator, matches-on keeps it, skip leaves defaults) + 4 new saver-guard tests (each hardened saver: absent ‚áí unchanged, present `"0"` ‚áí false). Parent spec ¬ß5/¬ß6/¬ß6.1 + TOTAL_STEPS=13 reconciled. **One pre-existing baseline failure surfaced and left alone:** `test_mentor_programme_toggle_saves_from_the_wizard` asserts `CommissionSetting::forAgency()->mentor_program_enabled` defaults true, but `forAgency` returns an UNSAVED model so the DB `DEFAULT 1` never applies ‚Äî confirmed identical on clean HEAD, untouched by this diff, flagged for Johan (a commission-config default bug, not a switchboard one). **Local test-DB note (again): XAMPP MariaDB is InnoDB-corrupt and won't start; Laragon MySQL 8.4.3 (`C:/laragon/data/mysql-8.4`, bin FIRST on PATH) is the working local DB ‚Äî neither auto-starts after reboot.** Spec `.ai/specs/agency-onboarding-feature-switchboard.md`. Branch `QA2`, NOT deployed. **The rule: a settings tree with a switch buried in each section is *working*; a guided, explained menu of the whole product that adapts the rest of setup to the choices made is the front door no competitor offers ‚Äî and "one home per switch" is what stops the two drifting.**

- **2026-07-17** ‚Äî **The P24 "Import All" was one browser tab hand-parallelised into eight, and going faster had been silently shipping listings with missing photos.** A live audit (`.ai/audits/p24-import-throughput-live-2026-07-17.md` ‚Äî written on the server, NOT yet committed to a branch I can see; flagged for commit) found the first ~4000-property go-live **lost ~11% of offered images, 2,549 of 23,124**, because the operator's 8 tabs √ó a 10-wide image pool ‚âà **80 concurrent** requests tripped P24's per-IP rate limiter ‚Äî and `DownloadP24RowImagesJob` ran `tries=1`, swallowed the rate-limit failures into a log line, and wrote whatever it managed as "done". Green job, empty `failed_jobs`, short galleries live on the site. Rebuilt the import as a two-lane queue architecture with **zero photo loss as the acceptance bar, not an aspiration**. The property write and the image download are split onto separate queues: **`p24import` WIDE (8 workers ‚Äî a DB write, no CDN, fan out hard: this is where the speed is) and `p24images` NARROW (4 workers ‚âà 40 concurrent to P24, deliberately under the ~80 that caused loss)**. The confirm no longer downloads inline (`dispatchSync`‚Üíasync `dispatch`), so a property is searchable in seconds while its gallery streams in behind and keeps going even if the tab closes. **The no-loss guarantee lives in the image job, now self-healing:** `tries=5`, fetches ONLY the ordinals not already on disk (a retry is cheap; a re-import refetches nothing), rebuilds the gallery from EVERY ordinal on disk (a recovered middle image closes the gap, not appended), `release()`s to retry while short, and only after exhausting tries records `incomplete` with a WARNING naming expected/stored/missing ‚Äî **it can never report `complete` while short**, which is the exact lie the old job told. New `properties` columns make completeness a queryable fact (`gallery_expected_count`/`gallery_stored_count`/`gallery_import_status`/`p24_source_image_signature` ‚Äî the INBOUND mirror of the outbound `p24_image_signature`, never conflate them), and an owner-only `/api/v1/importer/gallery-reconciliation` is the live proof of the bar: `short`/`incomplete`/`failed` must settle to 0 once the image lane drains. **Import All is now one server-side click** (`Bus::batch`, not a browser `for` loop) with a dual progress bar (properties from the batch, galleries from the columns so it survives a reload). **The real "Import All" is the public onboarding PORTAL, not the admin page** ‚Äî the admin `confirmBulk` route exists but no UI references it; the 8 tabs were 8 portal tabs. Found + fixed a latent bug on the way: the confirm job never set `branch_id` (NOT NULL, no default) and relied on `BelongsToBranch` auto-fill, which no-ops in a queued job with no auth user ‚Äî every imported property was one tightening away from 1364-ing. **The workers are half the feature: existing workers drain only `default`, so `p24import`/`p24images` jobs strand until Supervisor gets the two new blocks** (`docs/infra/supervisor/corex-worker-p24.conf`, apply steps included). **QA sites run no worker ‚Üí first real QA on Staging, not qa1/qa2.** Deliberately forward-only: no backfill of the ~11% already lost (separate remediation), but a re-import heals affected galleries for free via fetch-only-missing. `ParallelImportGalleryIntegrityTest` 10/10 (49 assertions) ‚Äî self-heal, can-never-report-complete-while-short, fetch-only-missing, unchanged-reimport-refetches-nothing, imageless‚Üícomplete, split-lane dispatch, batch, reconciliation owner-only. Local test note: **XAMPP MariaDB is corrupt (InnoDB LSN-in-future); Laragon MySQL 8.4.3 is the live local DB** and neither auto-starts after reboot. Spec `.ai/specs/importer.md` ¬ß14. Branch `QA2`, NOT deployed. **The rule, third of this family: a test (or a job) that asserts the shape you WISH the vendor sent proves nothing ‚Äî the old image job's only "success" was the shape P24 never sends under load.**

- **2026-07-17** ‚Äî **Agent invites moved to the last step of onboarding ‚Äî and the page I moved them TO had been silently broken for months.** Invites were sent from the agent **run detail** page, mid-import, which meant an agent could be invited into a CoreX **with no properties in it** ‚Äî and the first login is an impression you get exactly once. They now go out from **Property Onboarding** (`admin.importer.review`) as the final step. The placement is **structural, not procedural**: that page's cards only exist for agencies that already have listings, so "properties first" cannot be forgotten by whoever is doing the import. Scope is the **agency, not the run** ‚Äî an agency imported over two agent runs is still one agency to the person pressing the button, and making them know which run an agent arrived in is our problem leaking into their workflow. **What the move exposed matters more than the move.** Two defects had been sitting under the old per-run trickle, invisible precisely *because* it was a trickle: **nothing anywhere recorded that an invite had been sent** (no column existed), so a bulk button would cheerfully re-mail an entire agency on a second press; and `sendAllInvites` looped **`dispatchSync`**, sending every email inside the HTTP request ‚Äî fine for three agents one at a time, a guaranteed timeout for a 40-agent single press. Fixed both at the choke point: new **`users.invited_at`**, stamped inside `SendAgentInviteJob` **after** the notification is handed to the mailer (never at dispatch ‚Äî a failed send must not mark an agent invited), and since both the bulk and per-agent paths run through that one job, the two can never disagree about who has been invited. The job also gained the explicit **`$timeout`** whose absence is what let the 60s worker default SIGKILL `SyncAgentToP24Job` in June. **The real find, though, was a bug I wasn't looking for: the review page has always been silently broken for an owner who uses the agency switcher.** `User`, `P24ImportRun`, `P24OnboardingPortal` and `P24PortalEvent` are all tenant-scoped, and `AgencyScope` no-ops for an owner **only** while `session('active_agency_id')` is unset. Switch into any agency and every one of that page's queries returns an empty set ‚Äî it reports **"no agents"/"no portals" for an agency that has twenty, with no error, no 500, nothing to explain it**. The importer is owner-only and spans agencies **by design**, so scoping it to the viewer's own agency was never coherent. Fixed the **class** (every cross-agency query on the page drops the scope explicitly, SoftDeletes deliberately left ON so an archived agent drops out of the list and the counts) rather than just the code I was adding, and pinned it with a named regression test ‚Äî otherwise the next person to touch the page reintroduces it. **Bulk press is safe to repeat**: already-invited and already-active agents are skipped and **reported concretely** ("Skipped 3 already invited and 2 already active") instead of silently doing nothing, which is the difference between a button that looks broken and one that explains itself; re-sending stays a deliberate **per-agent** action for the bounced-email case. Prevent **and** absorb, not either: the button only renders when there is something to send, *and* the controller handles a press with nothing to send ‚Äî because a stale tab can post either way. **`users.email` is NOT NULL + UNIQUE**, so the only representable "no email" state is the empty string ‚Äî the guard tests `blank()`, and the test asserting otherwise failed against the schema, which is the test doing its job. **Consequence to plan around: invites are queued, and QA sites run no worker ‚Äî this feature gets its first honest QA on Staging, not qa1/qa2.** The flash says "queued" vs "sent" off `config('queue.default')` rather than claiming a send that hasn't happened. Spec `.ai/specs/importer.md` updated (¬ß4.1, ¬ß5.2 Agents, ¬ß6.2, ¬ß7 Stage 3, ¬ß11); `AgentInviteFromReviewTest` 13/13. **The rule: when a feature moves, the thing to fear is not the move ‚Äî it's the assumption the old placement was hiding.**

- **2026-07-17** ‚Äî **"The 11 stuck listings need a resubmit" was WRONG, and acting on it would have advertised sold houses.** Correcting my own call from earlier the same day. **All 11 rows sitting at `submitted` since 25 Jun are OFF-MARKET** ‚Äî 8 `withdrawn`, 1 `expired`, **2 `sold`**. P24 was not failing to activate them; **P24 was correctly refusing to show them** (`"This listing is blocked."`, `"Status is inactive."`, `"Expiry date must be in the future"`). A resubmit would have pushed withdrawn and **sold** properties back onto Property24 as live adverts ‚Äî the exact failure the mixed-case sweep called *"a worse failure than the rental badge"*. **The bug was never the listings; it was that `p24_syndication_status` was lying.** They are correctly off the portal; `submitted` just renders as "Submitted, awaiting activation‚Ä¶" forever. Fix = tell the truth (`deactivated`), **not** a resubmit. **The second claim was also wrong**: *"8 listings live on P24 while CoreX says otherwise"* came from **stale cached `p24_syndication_logs` rows** (#1405's last check was 11 Jul, #1724's 13 Jul). A **fresh authoritative sweep of all 252 suspect rows found ZERO stranded adverts** ‚Äî nothing is publicly live that shouldn't be. **The real structural hole:** `SyncProperty24Activations` only sweeps enabled listings at submitted/pending/active (**191 rows**); everything claiming to be OFF the portal (**252 rows**) was reconciled by **nothing** ‚Äî `p24:reconcile-portal-presence` existed but **was never scheduled**, so drift was only ever repaired when a human remembered to run it. Worse, its suspect set was **`deactivated` ALONE**, so **`error` (159) and `rejected` (30) were never checked by anything** ‚Äî 189 rows that read as "not advertised" while potentially hiding a live listing. Now: suspect set canonical on the model (**`Property::P24_CLAIMS_OFF_PORTAL_STATUSES`** = deactivated+error+rejected; deliberately excludes the hot set and excludes sold/rented, which legitimately stay ON the portal), **scheduled nightly 02:45**, and **deliberately WITHOUT `--withdraw`** ‚Äî it corrects status (no portal writes) and logs **`P24 STRANDED ADVERT`** naming anything live that should not be. **Auto-pulling a public advert on a cron is Johan's call, not a default ‚Äî open question for Johan.** Live remediation: **checked=252 already-correct=63 status-fixed=189 withdrawn=0 no-answer=0**; enabled listings now **193 active / 80 deactivated / 1 pending** ‚Äî no `error`/`rejected`/`submitted` lies left. Verified safe before applying: **0 stranded adverts** and **0 enabled on-market rows in the suspect set**, so `error‚Üídeactivated` hides no actionable failure. **This sweep only became safe today** ‚Äî it reads `isOnPortal()`, which returned `true` **unconditionally** until `70f72140`; running it before that would have marked every genuinely off-portal listing `active`. Hotfix `69fa4b01` on `main` (live) ‚Üí cherry-picked to Staging `d904d085`. **The rule: a status column is a CACHE, and a cached "submitted" is not evidence a listing is waiting on the portal ‚Äî ask the portal before you act on it, and never resubmit off-market stock to fix a UI label.** [[p24-is-on-portal-wire-format]]

- **2026-07-17** ‚Äî **The P24 activation reconcile has been a complete no-op, and ~137,000 API calls a week were resolving to nothing.** An agent reported property **#4791** "syncing for days". #4791 itself was a false alarm ‚Äî it was `let_out` with a **R 0 price** from 3 Jul, so CoreX correctly never pushed it (zero P24 calls in the whole window); the agent set a price and flipped it to `to_let` at 13:18 and it went live in 60 seconds. **The bug was what I found while proving that.** P24 answers `is-on-portal` as **text/plain with a PHP-style boolean cast** ‚Äî **`"1"` for true, an EMPTY body for false** (`(string) true === "1"`, `(string) false === ""`), and `request()` wraps non-JSON bodies as `['raw' => ‚Ä¶]`. `syncActivationStatus` compared that raw string against `true`/`'true'`/`'True'` with `===`, so **BOTH branches were unreachable for every real response**: 7 days of production logs held **137,766 status_checks carrying exactly two values** (`"1"` √ó127,023, `""` √ó10,743) **and changing nothing**. `"Property #X confirmed active on P24"` fired **11 times in the entire log window** ‚Äî only when P24 happened to send a JSON content-type. Consequence: a listing P24 **had activated** never left `submitted`, so the panel showed **"Submitted, awaiting activation‚Ä¶" indefinitely** ‚Äî which is precisely what an agent reads as *"stuck syncing"* ‚Äî and a listing P24 **had dropped** stayed `active` forever, the exact drift the reconcile exists to catch. Second bug in the same file: **`isOnPortal()` ‚Äî the delist guard, documented as "the ONLY trustworthy answer to is-it-still-live" ‚Äî did `(bool) ($result['data'] ?? false)` on the ARRAY `['raw' => '']`. A non-empty array is always truthy, so it answered YES for every listing**, including the ~10.7k weekly checks where P24 said the listing was off the portal. **Why it survived: the only test faked `Content-Type: application/json` with body `'true'` ‚Äî a shape P24 does not send** ‚Äî which decodes to a real bool and hit the one branch that worked. Green test, dead runtime; the same failure mode the e-sign moat exists to prevent. **Fix = parse the wire format ONCE, in the client that owns it** (`Property24ApiClient::interpretOnPortalPayload`), handing callers a normalised `true|false|null`; an unrecognised payload is now `null` = *"we don't know"* and **leaves the local status untouched + logs a warning**, rather than silently reading as "not on portal". **`""` ‚Üí false was verified, not assumed**: it is a **stable per-listing answer (288/288 consecutive checks)**, and **no currently-`active` listing returns it**, so the deploy demoted nothing ‚Äî confirmed by a forced pass (202 synced, 0 errors, **0 promotions, 0 demotions, 0 unrecognised**). Live proof of the guard: **#4791 ‚Üí true, #1386 ‚Üí false** (before the fix, *both* returned true). Hotfix `70f72140` on `main` (live `/corex`): fpm reload + `corex-worker-live` restart. **Tests owe a `dev-check.ps1` run on Windows ‚Äî no dev deps on the server** (`vendor/bin/phpunit` absent), so the new assertions are UNRUN; the fix was verified against live data + the live P24 API instead. **STILL OPEN, all pre-existing and NOT fixed by this:** (1) **11 listings stuck at `submitted` for 10‚Äì22 days** (1386, 5889, 4953, 5764, 3943, 3836, 4001, 5886, 2020, 5801, 5785) ‚Äî P24 genuinely does **not** have them; the reconcile is now honest about it but they need a **resubmit**, and nothing escalates a listing that never activates; (2) **8 listings are LIVE on P24 while CoreX says `rejected`/`error`/`deactivated`/`sold`** ‚Äî the "stranded on portal" class, and they sit **outside** the reconcile set; (3) `syncAllActivations` uses **scoped** `Property::` queries inside a queue job, silently skipping **6 other-agency listings** (202 visible vs 208 real) ‚Äî AgencyScope/BranchScope with no auth context; (4) **6,026 failed jobs**, dominated by `OversightNudgeMail` **√ó3,903** (`No hint path defined for [mail]`) and `SyncProperty24Activations` **√ó927** (timeouts). **The rule, and it is the third of this family after the two mixed-case enum bugs: a test that fakes a shape the vendor does not send proves nothing ‚Äî assert the payload the wire actually carries.** [[syndication-mapper-vocabulary-gotcha]]

- **2026-07-14** ‚Äî **AT-11: CoreX has been charging agencies money that the product could not name.** No price, no plan, no seat count anywhere in the schema ‚Äî the commercial relationship lived entirely in spreadsheets and memory. Built the money model plus the two pages that read it. **Four decisions Johan locked, because each one changes what we actually invoice:** (1) a **billable seat is any active, non-archived user** ‚Äî role is irrelevant, an admin occupies a seat exactly like an agent, and deactivating a leaver drops them off the next bill (this is the single biggest driver of the number, and "per agent" was ambiguous enough to have been guessed wrong); (2) the plan **auto-tracks headcount**, and the two plans are **price shapes, not feature sets** ‚Äî both get full access to everything, which resolved the collision where the pricing sheet capped Team at 10 users *and* started Agency "from 10" (at exactly 10, Team = R4 500 and Agency = R4 445, so "which plan?" had no answer until Johan gave one); (3) **no VAT anywhere**; (4) **custom amount and discount never coexist**. Extra branches are charged on **both** plans, first free ‚Äî Johan's call, and the right one: an 8-agent shop running two branches is on Team *and* pays R750 for the second, because charging R0 for a real branch is a revenue leak. **The design decision that matters more than any of the pricing: the seat count is counted LIVE on every read and never stored.** The bill therefore cannot be stale ‚Äî not after a bulk import, not after a raw SQL UPDATE, not after someone edits a user in tinker. Domain events and the nightly sweep exist **only to make the plan-change email prompt**, never to keep the number right; a dropped event costs a late email, never a wrong invoice. That split is what let the whole feature be robust without ceremony: the plan flip is a **compare-and-set**, so a page render racing the nightly sweep emails Johan **once**, not twice; and the discount **expires by arithmetic** (`starts_on + months`, never a stored end-date), so there is no cron that can forget to end it and no "why is this agency still on 20% off" three months from now. The custom-vs-discount invariant is guarded at three layers ‚Äî mode selector, validation, and custom-wins-on-read ‚Äî so a row hand-edited in SQL to hold both still produces a correct price rather than double-discounting; that path is asserted, not hoped for. **The developer page has no permission key on purpose**: a key is grantable through Role Manager, and one mis-click would show an agency admin every competitor's negotiated rate ‚Äî so it is `owner_only`, a role check, with a 403 test standing over it. **Re-hit a landmine AT-230 had already logged** and honoured its fix: a queued listener on a domain event fatals (`SerializesModels` can't restore `AbstractDomainEvent`'s parent readonly `$eventId` from the child scope), so the listener stays sync and queues a Job carrying **scalars only** ‚Äî which is the better payload regardless, since a job holding an Agency model would `ModelNotFoundException` on an agency archived between the switch and the send. **Deliberately NOT built: the payment gate itself** (AT-11 also asks for cutoff/lockout). It is specced as Phase 2 reusing the existing `maintenance_mode` lockout rather than a second mechanism ‚Äî you cannot build a credible gate before the system can say what is owed, and shipping half a gate would have been the "good enough for now" the Operating Principle forbids. 51 tests / 134 assertions. Spec `.ai/specs/agency-billing.md`. **Open for Johan: sign-off on the spec, and confirm ¬ß14 ‚Äî that NOTHING from this feature belongs in the onboarding wizard, because plan/discount/custom-amount are CoreX-side commercial terms, and a "your discount %" control in a customer's setup wizard would let them price themselves.**

- **2026-07-14** ‚Äî **Sixty SOLD properties were generating ad cards that advertised them "FOR SALE" ‚Äî and I only found it because I went to verify the rental fix on staging.** Pushing the rental hotfix to Staging, I rendered the fix against the staging DB as a sanity check and the badge came back reading a raw **"Active"**. That was the thread: **`properties.status` is mixed-case in production exactly like `listing_type`** ‚Äî the wizard writes lowercase, the **P24 sync writes capitalised** (`'Active'` **444 rows**, `'Sold'` **60**, `'Rented'` 1) ‚Äî and every badge compared it **case-sensitively** against lowercase lists. So `in_array($status, ['sold','transferred'], true)` **missed every `'Sold'` row**, fell through to the default arm, and badged it **"For Sale"** on the pickers and **"FOR SALE"** on generated ad cards. A sold house being marketed as for sale is a worse failure than the rental badge that started the session, and it was sitting there the whole time. Two further gaps closed with it: **`rented`/`let_out` appeared in no concluded-status list anywhere**, so a tenanted property badged **"To Let"** ‚Äî advertising an occupied home as available (they are the rental equivalent of `sold`; `isConcluded()` now covers all four); and the preview's badge map was keyed on the raw column with an `ucfirst()` fallback, so **1,703 listings** fell through and showed a client the internal DB value ‚Äî **"Let_out"**, **"Under_offer"**, **"For_sale"**, underscores and all. **`Property::normalizedStatus()` is now THE way to read status** ‚Äî the twin of `isRental()`, same cure, one place ‚Äî and `statusBadge()` (pickers), `adData()` (ad cards) and the preview badge all route through it. `pending` deliberately keeps its own "Pending" badge rather than collapsing into the For Sale / To Let base that `adData()` documents (Johan's call ‚Äî don't change what wasn't reported broken). Verified against live data across every stored casing: `'Sold'`‚ÜíSold/SOLD, `'Active'`+rental‚ÜíTo Let, `'Rented'`‚ÜíRented, `'let_out'`‚ÜíLet Out, `'under_offer'`‚ÜíUnder Offer, lowercase twins unchanged, 6075 still To Let. **The rule, now proven twice in one session: a CoreX enum column is not normalised on write ‚Äî never compare one case-sensitively, go through the model's canonical reader.** That is the third mixed-case bug of this family (the match-email leak was the first). Hotfix `de1c10bd` on `main` (live `/corex`), merged into `Staging` (`bfb0b842`, preserving another lane's AT-264); **tests still owe a `dev-check.ps1` run on Windows ‚Äî no dev deps on the server.**

- **2026-07-14** ‚Äî **A rental was advertised "For Sale" on the live preview ‚Äî and it was never one listing, it was 94.** Reported on property 6075 ("Penthouse ‚Ä¶ to let in Uvongo", `listing_type=rental`, `status=active`), whose live preview ‚Äî **the page an agent sends to a client** ‚Äî wore a "For Sale" badge. The blade mapped status‚Üíbadge with a hardcoded `'active' => 'For Sale'` and **never consulted `listing_type` at all**, so the badge was wrong for every active rental in the system; the reporter simply happened to open one of them. Two further sale-assumptions sat on the same page and shipped with the fix: the price card said **"Asking price"** over a monthly rent, and a **bond calculator** offered the tenant a repayment schedule for a purchase that will never happen ‚Äî seeded from the sale `price` column, which on a rental is 0/null, or (as on 6075) the rent, so it cheerfully costed a bond on R13,900. **The class beneath the instance is the real story.** "Is this a rental?" was answered **inline, in six places, with divergent vocabularies AND case-sensitive comparisons**: `statusBadge()` and `adData()` accepted `rental|to_let`; `effectivePrice()` lowercased but accepted only `rental`; the P24 and PP deep-link builders accepted only lowercase `rental` (so an imported rental deep-linked into P24's **`/for-sale/`** section); two blades rolled their own; the website API accepted `rental|to_let|to-let|lease`. Meanwhile **`P24ListingsCsvParser` writes a capitalised `'Rental'`** ‚Äî a spelling that fails *every* one of those checks, which would have rendered, badged, priced and deep-linked an imported rental as a sale. **`Property::isRental()` is now THE predicate** ‚Äî case-insensitive, trimmed, whole vocabulary, one place ‚Äî and all six callers route through it, so the surfaces can no longer disagree with each other. The case-tolerance is **preventive, and I'm saying so rather than claiming a save: 0 rows carry the capitalised spelling today.** But the importer that writes it is live, and the next import would have been the second instance of this exact bug. Verified by rendering the real view for 6075 (badge **To Let**, **Monthly rental R 13 900 / month**, calculator absent; the sale control still reads For Sale / Asking price and keeps its calculator), then confirmed on the live URL after a php8.4-fpm reload. **The preview page had no test at all ‚Äî which is precisely how a rental came to be advertised for sale and nobody noticed until a human opened the page.** `tests/Feature/Properties/PropertyLivePreviewListingTypeTest.php` now pins the badge, the price label, the calculator's absence, dead-status precedence over listing type, and the full `isRental()` vocabulary including the importer's casing. Hotfix on `main` (`dee61c28`, live `/corex`); **tests could not be run on the server ‚Äî no dev deps there ‚Äî so `dev-check.ps1` still owes them a run on Windows.**

- **2026-07-14** ‚Äî **P24 Refresh went slow again ‚Äî and it was the SAME bug, wearing the agent instead of the gallery.** Reported as "refresh was 60s+, we fixed it to 10s, now it's slow again". The image fix was never the problem and is still intact (verified on live: of 4,773 listings with a `p24_ref`, every one carrying a signature matched it ‚Äî **0 mismatches** ‚Äî so they all send `photos: null`). What had crept back in was commit `71b29f5b` (25 Jun, months AFTER the image fix): `ensureAgentRegisteredByUser` began **unconditionally** re-pushing the agent's full profile AND re-uploading their profile photo on **every** submit ‚Äî per agent, so a two-agent listing paid four P24 round-trips before the listing POST even started (live trace: property #2909 took 9s, of which ~8 were agent sync and 1 was the actual listing). Behind it sat the real 60s+ killer: that path calls `GET /agencies/{id}/agents`, a **610KB response that takes 15‚Äì90s** on P24's side and which **timed out at 120s on 2026-07-14 15:33** (`cURL error 28`) ‚Äî and because a failure is (correctly) never cached, **every** refresh re-paid the full timeout until one succeeded. Worse, `php artisan cache:clear` is **in our own deploy checklist**, so the 25h agent cache is cold after every deploy and the next agent to press Refresh ate the cold fetch. **Fix ‚Äî the rule, not the instance: never send a portal bytes it already holds.** Agent id now resolves from `users.p24_agent_id` + new `p24_agent_agency_id` (zero HTTP; the users table survives `cache:clear`, which is why the cache is now an optimisation, not a dependency), and new `p24_profile_signature` / `p24_photo_signature` gate the profile PUT and the photo upload exactly the way `p24_image_signature` gates the gallery. `getAgents` additionally **serves a 30-day last-known-good list** on failure behind a 5-min breaker, so a sick P24 endpoint can never again block a refresh. Agency-scoped on purpose (P24 scopes agents per agency; a bare id would address the wrong agent for a co-listing under another branch). **Measured on live, property #6073: was 17s (first) / 6s (repeat) ‚Üí now 4s once, then 1 call in 0.9s** ("unchanged ‚Äî gallery and agents skipped"), with no agent-list scan at all. **The lasting part is the guard, because cost is invisible to a green pipeline** ‚Äî a slow refresh breaks no assertion, which is exactly how this shipped twice: (1) runtime ‚Äî `auditRefreshCost()` counts the P24 calls of every submit and logs **`P24 REFRESH COST REGRESSION`** naming the offending calls when an unchanged refresh exceeds its **one-call budget**; (2) build ‚Äî `tests/Feature/Syndication/Property24RefreshCostTest.php` asserts that budget outright, asserts the agent list is never scanned, and asserts a genuinely changed photo IS still re-uploaded (the gate must not become a wall); (3) gate ‚Äî `dev-check.ps1` ¬ß7 fails any portal-sync change landing without a `tests/Feature/Syndication/` diff. Contract written up in `.ai/specs/p24-syndication.md` + CLAUDE.md. Hotfix on `main` (live `/corex`); **tests could not be run on the server ‚Äî no dev deps there ‚Äî so `dev-check.ps1` still owes them a run on Windows.**

- **2026-07-13** ‚Äî **Duplicate Property was a hard 500 for EVERY property, and the null came from our own code.** `PropertyController::duplicate()` set `$clone->price = null` on purpose ‚Äî the copy is meant to start with no price so the agent must set one ‚Äî but `properties.price` is `bigint unsigned NOT NULL DEFAULT 0`, and **an explicit NULL into a NOT NULL column throws 1048 no matter what the default is** (the default only applies when the column is OMITTED from the INSERT; Eloquent sends every dirty attribute, so it sent `price = NULL`). Reported on property 6088, whose own price was a perfectly good 4710 ‚Äî the data was never the problem, so this was never a one-listing quirk: **duplicate had a 0% success rate.** Fix: `price = 0`. That is this schema's "unset" (604 rows carry it, **not one row is NULL**), and `empty(0)` is true, so `publishToggle()`'s readiness gate still lists **Price** as missing and the copy cannot go live until the agent sets a real one ‚Äî original intent preserved, with a value the column actually accepts. Same class as the AT-202/AT-203 `agency_id` NOT-NULL landmine: **a NOT-NULL column plus a writer that writes an explicit null.** Also wrapped the clone + its contact-link copy in `DB::transaction` (a half-copied property with no seller attached is worse than no copy), and **added the missing `use Illuminate\Support\Facades\DB;`** ‚Äî the file's only other `DB::` call is written `\DB::` fully-qualified, so an unqualified `DB::` would have resolved to `App\Http\Controllers\CoreX\DB` and fatalled at runtime; **`php -l` cannot catch that**, only executing the path can. Verified by driving the real `duplicate()` method against live property 6088 inside a rolled-back transaction: 302 ‚Üí clone is a `draft`, `price` 0, `published_at` null, P24/PP syndication off, contact links copied, `agency_id` preserved. Pinned by `tests/Feature/Properties/PropertyDuplicateTest.php`, including a test that the DB itself rejects a null price so nobody "helpfully" restores the old line.

- **2026-07-13** ‚Äî **A photo the user picked is either uploaded or explained. Never silently dropped.** The Add-Listing wizard filtered its selection with `f.size <= 5*1024*1024` and then `if (!images.length) return;` ‚Äî so when every photo exceeded 5MB (routine: listing photography runs 6‚Äì15MB) the filter emptied the array and the function returned **before issuing the request**. No POST, no error, no spinner: the agent clicked Upload and the page did not react. It read as a dead button, and the agent's workaround was to re-upload one photo at a time. **The cap itself was also simply wrong** ‚Äî the wizard enforced 5MB (`max:5120`) while the property page it feeds allowed 500MB (`max:512000`), so the same photo was accepted in one place and refused in the other. Settled on **one ceiling, 200MB, everywhere** (Johan's call): `max:204800` on the wizard AND on `store`/`update`/`uploadImages`/`uploadRentalImages`, mirrored by both client-side `MAX_FILE` consts. A per-file cap that differs by entry point is a bug generator, so the number matters far less than the fact that there is now exactly one of it. Note the 500MB batch bounds left in the blades are a different thing ‚Äî they bound the POST **envelope** under `post_max_size` (~550M), not the file. **The deeper lesson is the silence, not the number.** A client-side filter that discards input without saying so converts a validation failure into a phantom bug: nothing in any log, nothing on screen, and a user who reasonably concludes the software is broken. Every reject path now names the file and the reason, and step 2 gained the error banner it never had. The client's type/size checks deliberately mirror Laravel's `image` rule so an unsupported file (HEIC ‚Äî common on a Windows laptop holding iPhone photos) is refused *before* it can fail a batch server-side and take its valid siblings down with it. **Same class, second instance, fixed too:** the property-page uploader asked for `Accept: text/html`, so a validation failure came back as a `back()->withErrors` **302** ‚Äî which XHR follows transparently, landing on 200, which its `status < 400` check read as success ‚Äî *and that invisible redirect-follow consumed the flashed error bag*, so the `location.reload()` that followed rendered a clean page with no errors on it. A rejected upload looked exactly like a successful one. It now requests JSON and reads a real 422, and treats `added === 0` (PHP dropped the files before Laravel saw them) as the error it is. **Neither uploader had a single test** ‚Äî which is precisely how a 5MB cap on a real-estate photo tool shipped and survived; `PropertyPhotoUploadTest` now pins both.

- **2026-07-12** ‚Äî **The demo invitation now goes out as `mail@corexos.co.za`, not `system@hfcoastal.co.za`.** `DemoAccessGrantMail` ‚Äî the only delivery of a prospect's access code and login email ‚Äî was sent on the **default** mailer, which authenticates as `system@hfcoastal.co.za`: the **agency's** mailbox. It is a CoreX *product* invitation to a `corexos.co.za` demo, and the first thing a prospect ever sees of CoreX, so it now goes over the existing **`corex` mailer** (`Mail::mailer('corex')` in `SendDemoAccessGrantEmail`, the same mailer the agency-onboarding and user-invite mails already use). Nothing new was configured: `config/mail.php`'s `corex` block and the `MAIL_COREX_*` credentials were already in `.env` on live **and** staging. **The From is read from that mailer's own config block** (`mail.mailers.corex.from_address`), not hardcoded and not left to the global `mail.from` ‚Äî the header and the SMTP account that authenticates must always come from the same place, because a From that doesn't match the authenticated account fails SPF and the recipient's server bins the mail with **nothing raised our side**. **The non-obvious bit:** the mailer can only be pinned at the CALL SITE, not in the Mailable's constructor. This Mailable is `ShouldQueue`, and `Mailer::queue()` stamps the sending mailer's own name onto the mailable on its way to the queue ‚Äî a constructor pin would be silently overwritten, i.e. reassuring dead code. Any NEW call site that mails this must therefore select `corex` itself; `DemoAccessGrantTest::test_the_invitation_is_sent_from_the_corex_account_over_the_corex_mailer` asserts both halves (mailer + envelope From). Default sender for every other CoreX email is **unchanged**. Verified on live: the `corex` transport connects and authenticates as `mail@corexos.co.za`, and the envelope resolves to `mail@corexos.co.za (CoreX OS)`. Deployed to `/corex` (`d8b448bd`): view/route clear ‚Üí php8.3-fpm reload ‚Üí `queue:restart` (**required** ‚Äî the workers hold the old Mailable class in memory and it is the worker, not FPM, that builds the envelope).

- **2026-07-12** ‚Äî **`BelongsToAgency` was silently converting GLOBAL reference rows into agency-1 rows on single-agency installs ‚Äî this is what broke the demo deploy.** The `main` deploy ran clean on live and died on demo at `deploy:sync-reference-data` with `1062 Duplicate entry '1-mandate_expiry' for key 'cecs_agency_class_unique'`. Root cause is **not** the seeder: `BelongsToAgency`'s console/seeder fallback ("if exactly ONE agency exists in the DB, stamp it") was overwriting an **explicit `agency_id => null`**. `CalendarEventClassSeeder` writes its class defaults as GLOBAL rows (`agency_id` NULL) ‚Äî on `corex_demo`, which has exactly one agency, every one of those was written as an **agency-1** row instead. The seeder's next run looked for its global rows via `whereNull('agency_id')`, found none, re-inserted, and collided with the agency-1 rows it had created itself. **Live has agencies 1 and 7, so the fallback was never armed there** ‚Äî which is precisely why this shipped unnoticed: the environment that breaks is the one with fewer tenants. **Two consequences beyond the crash:** (1) on a single-agency install `deploy:sync-reference-data` could **never** provision the global reference rows it exists to provision (AT-162's whole purpose); (2) the seeder's `behaviourMap` / `occupies_time` / `autofill_buyers` reassertions are all scoped `whereNull('agency_id')`, so on demo they matched **zero rows** ‚Äî meaning demo's `viewing` class sat on the `freeform` column default and never offered "Capture Feedback to Complete". **Fix (root, in the trait):** an explicit null `agency_id` is now honoured as a deliberate global row and the fallback is skipped, distinguished from "caller never mentioned `agency_id`" by the attribute's **presence** in `getAttributes()` ‚Äî so the NOT-NULL crash-guard the fallback exists for still fires for seeders that simply omit the column. `DataDictionaryEntry` (the other two reference seeders) was never affected: it deliberately does not use the trait, for exactly this reason. Pinned by `tests/Feature/MultiTenancy/GlobalReferenceRowStampTest.php` (3/3 ‚Äî explicit-null survives, omitted-still-stamps, and the seeder is re-runnable on a single-agency DB); `AgencyIdWriterStampTest` 4/4 unchanged. **Demo needs a one-time repair** (see ¬ß5): its calendar class rows are still agency-1 rows, so they must be converted back to global (`UPDATE calendar_event_class_settings SET agency_id = NULL WHERE agency_id = 1`) ‚Äî no global row exists to collide with ‚Äî and the fixed seeder then reasserts the behaviour map onto them.

- **2026-07-12** ‚Äî **Dev Settings adopts the settings-hub shell; the Demo access card comes off it.** Dev Settings had drifted into its own layout (flat card stack) while every other settings surface in CoreX is the hub: dark header ‚Üí searchable rail ‚Üí `activeSection` panes. It now reuses that shell verbatim (`devSettingsHub()` mirrors `settingsHub()`; identical rail markup, tokens, and `?s=` deep-link contract), grouped **Overrides** (compliance-checks bypass) and **Demo** (demo-mode auth bypass + password gate, Demo Sidebar link). **The one non-obvious decision:** a single `<form>` wraps the whole right pane rather than one form per pane ‚Äî `DevSettingsController@update` writes BOTH dev keys on every submit and relies on each checkbox's hidden `"0"` sibling, and `x-show` hides panes without unmounting them, so the hidden pane's value still posts. Split the forms and saving Demo would silently clear the compliance override. **Demo access card removed** (Johan's call, this prompt): it was owner sales tooling advertised inside a dev-overrides page, and it already has its own owner-only sidebar entry ‚Äî routes, controller, and the page itself are untouched, only the card is gone, pinned by `test_dev_settings_index_no_longer_advertises_demo_access`. Password-gate failures redirect to `?s=demo` so the error is on the pane that raised it, not on Compliance. `DemoSidebarCurationTest` 13/13.

- **2026-07-12** ‚Äî **QA2 ‚Üí Staging: the two demo rebuilds CONVERGED into one (Johan's call at the merge).** Staging and QA2 had each independently diagnosed *the same* fault ‚Äî the demo was destroying itself nightly ‚Äî and each shipped its own 3-day rebuild: Staging's **`demo:refresh`** and AT-230's **`demo:reset`**. The merge auto-carried **BOTH**, each `dailyAt('03:00')` under a **different `withoutOverlapping()` name** (`demo-refresh` vs `demo-access.reset`) ‚Äî so nothing would have stopped two full wipes racing on the same box on the same night. They also asserted **contradictory facts about the same host**: Staging's comment said the demo box is `APP_ENV=demo`; AT-230 said it runs `APP_ENV=production` (and ships a passing test to that effect). **RESOLUTION ‚Äî one schedule, best-of-both:** the surviving entry is `demo:reset --scheduled`, because it alone has (a) the **right gate**, `Instance::isDemo()`/`COREX_INSTANCE_ROLE`, which does **not** consult `APP_ENV` and therefore holds on a demo box running `APP_ENV=production` ‚Äî the exact trap that made `DemoLoginController::isEnabled()` false on the demo host; (b) the **right timing**, `DemoResetSchedule::isResetDay()`, a pure function of time that is *the same function the countdown banner reads*, so the banner cannot promise a reset the scheduler will not perform (it replaces `demo:refresh`'s stored `lastRefreshedAt` throttle, which lived in the database the reset destroys); and (c) the **right target** ‚Äî a demo *instance* rebuilding its own default DB, whereas `demo:refresh` targets a dedicated `demo` connection, the right shape for rebuilding a demo DB from *another* box. **`demo:refresh`'s one real advantage was ported across, not lost:** it never destroyed anything it had not first dumped, so `demo:reset` now **backs up before the wipe and REFUSES to wipe if the backup fails** (prevent, don't absorb ‚Äî an unbacked demo rebuild is unrecoverable), with the same `demo.refresh.backup_path`/`keep_backups` rotation. Pinned by `test_a_failed_backup_prevents_the_wipe` (10/10 in `DemoResetScheduleTest`), which proves the tables survive **on a demo instance** ‚Äî i.e. with the `isDemo` guard passed, so the backup is genuinely the last thing between the command and `migrate:fresh`. `demo:refresh` is **retained as a hand-runnable command** (no hard deletes) but is **no longer scheduled** ‚Äî ‚öÝÔ∏è whoever deploys demo1 must know that. Also resolved: `config/corex-permissions.php` admin `exclude` ‚Äî kept Staging's **lift** of the `calendar.tile.my_deals` DR2 hold (AT-216 R3, Johan's explicit ask) *and* QA2's new owner-only `agency_setup.track` exclusion. **`database/schema/mysql-schema.sql` was NOT hand-merged** (again): the two snapshots came from differently-drifted DBs and **neither was a superset** (Staging alone had `agency_service_provider_contacts` + `deal_step_comments`; QA2 alone had `agency_onboarding_setups` + the six `demo_*`). Regenerated by loading Staging's snapshot into a **virgin schema**, letting the migrator replay QA2's 9 missing migrations, and re-dumping ‚Üí **436 tables, 0 removed, both sides intact**. GOTCHA (self-inflicted, worth not repeating): `git worktree remove --force` **follows a directory junction** and emptied the real `vendor/` through a link created inside the worktree ‚Äî recovered with `composer install`, but never junction `vendor` into a throwaway worktree.

- **2026-07-11** ‚Äî **AT-230 DEMO ACCESS CONTROL ‚Äî BUILT, AND THE SPEC WAS WRITTEN TO MATCH (review needed).** The build prompt cited `.ai/specs/demo-access-control.md` ¬ß4.1/¬ß6.2/¬ß6.7/¬ß11 as "the contract" ‚Äî **the file did not exist**, in the working tree or in any git ref. Per the Spec-First Rule the build stopped; on Johan's instruction the spec was **authored from the prompt + direct codebase investigation** and the build ran against it. **`¬ß0` of the new spec is a table of the 12 contracts Claude invented and needs Johan's sign-off** ‚Äî the schemas, the endpoint shapes, the credential form (email + 16-char code), the 5 event names, and one deliberate deviation: **archive is an explicit `archived_at` column, not Laravel `SoftDeletes`**, because `SoftDeletes` installs a global scope that hides rows from every default query and that is the wrong default for a table whose purpose is legal evidence (`SELECT COUNT(*)` must never decrease). DECISIONS: durable records live on **primary** (the demo DB is destroyed every 3 days, so telemetry stored there would delete itself); a new **`COREX_INSTANCE_ROLE`** flag is the security predicate, because **neither existing flag works** ‚Äî `config('app.env_label')` is cosmetic, and `DemoLoginController::isEnabled()` requires `!environment('production')` while **the demo host runs `APP_ENV=production`**, making it false on the very box it describes (the pre-existing `demo:cleanup`/`demo:seed` schedule in `routes/console.php` has therefore **never fired on demo** ‚Äî left in place for local, superseded by the `Instance::isDemo()`-gated `demo:reset`); grant status is **derived not stored** (no cron can keep a stored one honest, and a cron that "fixes" statuses can fail silently and re-admit an expired prospect); the reset is a **pure function of time** (a stored "next reset" row lives in the DB the reset destroys, and a *deferrable* countdown lies to everyone watching it). GOTCHAS worth keeping: **a queued listener on any CoreX domain event fatals** (`SerializesModels` can't restore `AbstractDomainEvent`'s parent-declared readonly `$eventId` from a child scope) ‚Äî queue the *Mailable*, not the listener; **appending middleware to the `web` group does NOT put it before `auth`** ‚Äî the priority list hoists `Authenticate`, and `prependToPriorityList` must anchor on the **contract** `Illuminate\Contracts\Auth\Middleware\AuthenticatesRequests`, not `Authenticate::class` (which matches nothing and no-ops silently); **`php artisan schema:dump` reads the stale local dev DB and silently DELETED 3 tables** from the committed snapshot ‚Äî always `DB_DATABASE=hfc_dash_test php artisan schema:dump`, then assert `git diff ‚Ä¶ | grep -c "^-CREATE TABLE"` is **0**. 58 tests / 197 assertions. NOT deployed. Spec ¬ß15 ordering: **mint the AgencyApiKey on primary BEFORE flipping demo's role**, or the gate fails closed and locks everyone out.

## 5. Outstanding small fixes (none blocking)

- **OPEN (2026-07-12) ‚Äî demo's calendar event-class rows are still agency-1 rows and need a one-time conversion to global.** The `BelongsToAgency` fix stops NEW global rows being stamped, but demo's existing `calendar_event_class_settings` were already written as agency-1 rows, and no global rows exist alongside them. Until they are converted, the seeder's `behaviourMap` / `occupies_time` / `autofill_buyers` updates (all `whereNull('agency_id')`) keep matching zero rows on demo ‚Äî so `viewing` stays on the `freeform` default and demo never offers "Capture Feedback to Complete". Repair on the demo box, AFTER pulling the fix, BEFORE `deploy:sync-reference-data`: `UPDATE calendar_event_class_settings SET agency_id = NULL WHERE agency_id = 1;` (safe ‚Äî no global row exists to collide with the unique key; no delete, the rows are converted in place, and demo is single-agency so nothing else resolves against agency 1). Then re-run the deploy: the seeder finds its global rows, updates them in place, and reasserts the behaviour map.

Confirmed PRE-EXISTING: fails identically on a clean tree with all SS-COMPLEX-IDENTITY changes stashed ‚Äî NOT introduced by the batch. Likely an auth/middleware/version-state redirect in the review controller. The batch's only edit to this file is the label-assertion string (now "Unit 8, Seeskulp"), which is correct for when the route issue is resolved. Needs a separate investigation of why the review route redirects in the test harness.
- **RESOLVED (2026-06-18) ‚Äî GPS-BORROW-FIX deployed + all scratch files deleted.** The geo fix (`64cfeb6f`) rode into Staging on the SS-COMPLEX-IDENTITY fast-forward and is now live on `/corex-staging`. All 6 `storage/tmp_*.php` scratch files (dev + staging) plus the staging `.bak` and shell-paste artifacts have been deleted; both checkouts are clean (only the legitimate `storage/framework/cache/` remains untracked).
